Case 23694: 05/04/2017 dict=MW, L= 110540, hw=nizam, user=geymonat

Case 4949: 9/2/2015 dict=MW, L=48545, hw=कारणा, user=zaaf2
old = [कारणात्, from some cause or reason, Rprāt.  iii, 13 Mn.  viii, 355 ; कस्मात् कारणात्, from what cause? मम-कारणात्, for my sake R.  &c ; अ-कारणेन, without a reason Yājñ.  ii, 234 ; येन कारणेन, because ; यस्मिन् कारणे, from which motive, wherefore.]
new = I think this should appear under कारण 1 n. ― This kind of problem results from the fact that in this new version of the dictionary (contrary to the printed edition and to former digital versions) the feminine and other forms of the same word are shown as separate entries, as if it were unconnected with the headword. I think this unjustifiable and misleading, first because it does not render the original structure of the article as in the printed edition (and surely the author had good reasons for that); secondly because it does not enhance the accessibility, since in reading and in research it is useful to have at a glance the full range of forms and meanings a word has acquired throughout its history, without having to do another search in the sidebar to see if there are other forms of the same word. Of course it is only my personal opinion. I only think the former synoptic display method better, and less prone to this kind of inconsistency or error, as here.  Thank you.
comment = Article structure
status =  Corrected 9/03/2015
------------------------------------------------------------------------

Case 4919: 7/11/2015 dict=MW, L=150361, hw=bhAvanA, user=geymonat
old = The electronic version is somewhat misleading as it splits the entry bhAvanA into two different pages one under bhAvana the other under bhAvanA
new = Repeat the first part of the definition of bhAvanA, that is given under bAvana after the value as a masculine, before the present definition of bhAvanA, in order to have the complete meaning of the lemma bhAvanA under one's eyes when one searches for it (in the present situation when bhAvanA is searched for as such, one gets only the meanings exclusively femminine, which are in fact less important than the ones occurring in the neuter gender also.) In fact the actual dictionary page has before the meanings of bhAvanA/am and immediately following, the meanings of bhAvanA N.B. The dictionary distinguishes the first set of meanings of bhAvanA from the second set of meanings, and so doing produces two apparently different entries, because with the first set of meanings the stem is found also as a neuter, as bhAvanam; but with the second set of meanings  the stem is only feminine bhAvanA. Another possibility would be to remove all together the entry bhAvanA and place the definition of bhAvanA only feminine under the entry bhAvana, after bhAvanA/am is given (and this is exactly what the dictionary does, so it might be the best thing to do in fact: but the beginner might be penalized by the fact that typing bhAvanA in the search box he would be replied that the entry doesn't exist, something which is obviously false)
comment = The stem bhAvanA has been split into two different entries one of which (the one that has the most usual meanings) is obtainable only typing in the search box bhAvana, the other by converse is seen only when one writes bhAvanA in the search box
status =  Commented 08/02/2015.  See experimental display //www.sanskrit-lexicon.uni-koeln.de/scans/awork/apidev/sample/testmw-0.1.html
